      <article class="post-12602 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-web-development tag-php tag-php-string-functions-cheat-sheet tag-php-string-functions-list" id="post-12602">
       <header class="entry-header">
        <h1 class="entry-title">
         <a href="http://vegibit.com/php-string-functions/" rel="bookmark">
          The Ultimate PHP String Functions List
         </a>
        </h1>
        <div class="entry-meta">
        </div>
        <!-- .entry-meta -->
       </header>
       <!-- .entry-header -->
       <div class="entry-content">
        <p>
         <img alt="php string functions list" class="alignleft size-full wp-image-12718" height="333" src="http://vegibit.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/php-string-functions-list.jpg" width="400"/>
        </p>
        <p class="lead">
         Welcome to the Ultimate PHP String Functions List. You can find all kinds php string functions tutorial articles online, however this php string functions cheat sheet will be the ultimate guide to using string functions in php. We took an exhaustive approach in coming up with the list and sorted the entire list based on frequency of use in the PHP community, usefulness, and importance of learning with regard to your php development. You can use this list to study for php string functions interview questions, or just to brush up on your own skills for self improvement. However you use the list is up to you. Now Lets dig in to the ultimate list of php string functions.
        </p>
        <hr/>
        When youre starting with PHP, its so easy to be overwhelmed by the sheer number of functions available to you. In this episode we happen to be studying php strings. Now what makes this list useful, maybe even more useful than just the list the documentation provides, is that we ran a program over the top php repositories online today and found out how many times each of these functions was used overall. This tells us what functions the pros are using, so it makes sense to focus on the ones that are giving the most mileage to them. That means the php string functions we have here, especially the ones near the top of the list, are extremely useful and will be the ones that we first learn and commit to memory.
        <hr/>
        <h2>
         1. substr()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           substr()
          </code>
          function returns a part of a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         If you know where the information that you want lies in a larger string, you can extract it out with the
         <code>
          substr()
         </code>
         function.
        </p>
        <h3>
         substr function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           substr
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, start, length
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to return a part of
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             start
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies where to start in the string
            <ul>
             <li>
              A positive number  Start at a specified position in the string
             </li>
             <li>
              A negative number  Start at a specified position from the end of the string
             </li>
             <li>
              0  Start at the first character in string
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             length
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies the length of the returned string.  Default is to the end of the string.
            <ul>
             <li>
              A positive number  The length to be returned from the start parameter
             </li>
             <li>
              Negative number  The length to be returned from the end of the string
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d3f40401019721" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
           &lt;?php
$sentence = "The Apple iPhone 6 Plus is cool, just don't bend it";
$one = substr($sentence, 9, 10); 
$two = substr($sentence, 24, 27); 

echo $one.' - ';
echo $two;
?&gt;
          </textarea>
         </div>

        <h2>
         2. strlen()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strlen()
          </code>
          function returns to us the number of characters in the string its given.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         There are many times when you will need to know the length of a string.  The
         <code>
          strlen()
         </code>
         function makes this super easy for us.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strlen function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strlen
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. This is the string that we will check the length of.
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

        <h2>
         3. sprintf()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           sprintf()
          </code>
          function returns a string created by filling
          <em>
           format
          </em>
          with the given arguments.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         The
         <code>
          sprintf()
         </code>
         function can be used to assign a formatted string to a variable.  The
         <strong>
          arg1
         </strong>
         ,
         <strong>
          arg2
         </strong>
         ,
         <strong>
          ++
         </strong>
         parameters are inserted at the percent
         <strong>
          (%)
         </strong>
         signs in the main string.
         <code>
          sprintf()
         </code>
         works in a step by step fashion meaning at the first
         <strong>
          %
         </strong>
         sign,
         <strong>
          arg1
         </strong>
         is inserted, at the second
         <strong>
          %
         </strong>
         sign,
         <strong>
          arg2
         </strong>
         is inserted, and so on.
        </p>
        <h3>
         sprintf function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           sprintf
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           format, arg1, arg2, arg++
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             format
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string and how to format the variables in it.
            <p>
             Possible format values:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              %%  Returns a percent sign
             </li>
             <li>
              %b  Binary number
             </li>
             <li>
              %c  The character according to the ASCII value
             </li>
             <li>
              %d  Signed decimal number (negative, zero or positive)
             </li>
             <li>
              %e  Scientific notation using a lowercase (e.g. 1.2e+2)
             </li>
             <li>
              %E  Scientific notation using a uppercase (e.g. 1.2E+2)
             </li>
             <li>
              %u  Unsigned decimal number (equal to or greather than zero)
             </li>
             <li>
              %f  Floating-point number (local settings aware)
             </li>
             <li>
              %F  Floating-point number (not local settings aware)
             </li>
             <li>
              %g  shorter of %e and %f
             </li>
             <li>
              %G  shorter of %E and %f
             </li>
             <li>
              %o  Octal number
             </li>
             <li>
              %s  String
             </li>
             <li>
              %x  Hexadecimal number (lowercase letters)
             </li>
             <li>
              %X  Hexadecimal number (uppercase letters)
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             Additional format values. These are placed between the % and the letter (example %.2f):
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              + (Forces both + and  in front of numbers. By default, only negative numbers are marked)
             </li>
             <li>
               (Specifies what to use as padding. Default is space. Must be used together with the width specifier. Example: %x20s (this uses x as padding)
             </li>
             <li>
               (Left-justifies the variable value)
             </li>
             <li>
              [0-9] (Specifies the minimum width held of to the variable value)
             </li>
             <li>
              .[0-9] (Specifies the number of decimal digits or maximum string length)
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note:
             </strong>
             If multiple additional format values are used, they must be in the same order as above.
            </p>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             arg1
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. The argument to be inserted at the first %-sign in the format string
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             arg2
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. The argument to be inserted at the second %-sign in the format string
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             arg++
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. The argument to be inserted at the third, fourth, etc. %-sign in the format string
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d3f60225538097" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">

        <h2>
         4. echo()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           echo()
          </code>
          function outputs strings and information to the browser.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Youll make use of
         <code>
          echo()
         </code>
         constantly.  Technically,
         <code>
          echo()
         </code>
         is not actually a function but a language construct.  As such, in almost all use cases you will omit the parenthesis entirely.
        </p>
        <h3>
         echo function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           echo
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           strings
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             strings
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. One or more strings to be sent to the output
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>

$verb = 'am chilling';
$state = 'cool';

    echo "&lt;span class='label label-info'&gt;Why yes, Yes it is $person.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;";
?&gt;

        <h2>
         5. strpos()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strpos()
          </code>
          function returns the position of the first occurrence of
          <strong>
           find
          </strong>
          in
          <strong>
           string
          </strong>
          . If specified, the function begins its search at position
          <strong>
           start
          </strong>
          . Returns false if
          <strong>
           find
          </strong>
          is not found.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         You can use the
         <code>
          strpos()
         </code>
         function to find the first occurrence of a small string in a larger string and if the small string isnt found,
         <code>
          strpos()
         </code>
         returns false.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strpos function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strpos
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, find, start
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             find
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to find
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             start
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies where to begin the search
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

         Code Example
        </h4>

        <p>
         The code above uses a string of characters that represent numbers as a string.  These are not real numbers, they are of type string not int or float!  We simply use this to illustrate that when using this function the very first character in a string starts with zero.  For every single character including any whitespace, the number increments by one.  We start at the first position of 0 in the example, but had we started at 8 for example, then the function would have returned false since it was looking for 7, but started looking at the eighth position so it already missed it.
        </p>

        <h2>
         6. implode()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           implode()
          </code>
          function does the exact opposite of
          <code>
           explode()
          </code>
           it creates a large string from an array of smaller strings.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns a string created by joining every element in the array with separator.
        </p>
        <h3>
         implode function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           implode
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           separator, array
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             separator
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies what to put between the array elements. Default is  (an empty string)
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             array
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Required. The array to join to a string
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

$fields = array('iPhone', 'Macbook', 'Lenovo Ultrabook', 'Vacation at Cape Cod');
$string = implode(' @@ ', $fields);

echo $string;

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         7. str_replace()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           str_replace()
          </code>
          function replaces some characters with some other characters in a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Searches for all occurrences of
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         in string and replaces them with
         <b>
          replace
         </b>
         . If all three parameters are strings, a string is returned. If string is an array, the replacement is performed for every element in the array and an array of results is returned. If
         <b>
          find
         </b>
         and
         <b>
          replace
         </b>
         are both arrays, elements in
         <b>
          find
         </b>
         are replaced with the elements in
         <b>
          replace
         </b>
         with the same numeric indices. Finally, if
         <b>
          find
         </b>
         is an array and
         <b>
          replace
         </b>
         is a string, any occurrence of any element in
         <b>
          find
         </b>
         is changed to
         <b>
          replace
         </b>
         . If supplied,
         <strong>
          count
         </strong>
         is filled with the number of instances replaced.
        </p>
        <h3>
         str_replace function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           str_replace
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           find, replace, string, count
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             find
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the value to find
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             replace
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the value to replace the value in
            <em>
             find
            </em>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to be searched
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             count
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A variable that counts the number of replacements
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d3f78366796524" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
           &lt;?php
$strings = array (
        'You like to have a great experience',
        'You are a really nice individual',
        'Do you like to drink Dunkin Donuts?' 
);
 
$search = array (
        'great',
        'experience',
        'individual',
        'Dunkin Donuts' 
);
$replace = array (
        'fantastic',
        'time',
        'person',
        'Starbucks' 
);
 
$replaced = str_replace ( $search, $replace, $strings );
 
print_r ( $replaced );
?&gt;
          </textarea>

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         8. strtolower()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strtolower()
          </code>
          function turns a mixed case string into all lowercase characters.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         with all alphabetic characters converted to lowercase. The table used for converting characters is locale-specific.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strtolower function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strtolower
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string that we will convert to all lowercase.
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d3f7e857196481" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
           &lt;?php
function chill($string) {
    
    return strtolower ( $string );
}
 
$person = 'BUDDY CAN YOU TURN OFF THE CAPS LOCK KEY?!';
 
echo chill ( $person );
?&gt;
          </textarea>

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         9. explode()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           explode()
          </code>
          function breaks apart a string into an array.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         If you know where the information that you want lies in a larger string, you can extract it out with the
         <code>
          explode()
         </code>
         function.
        </p>
        <h3>
         explode function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           explode
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           separator, string, limit
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             separator
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies where to break the string
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. The string to split
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             limit
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies the number of array elements to return.
            <p>
             Possible values:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              Greater than 0  Returns an array with a maximum of
              <em>
               limit
              </em>
              element(s)
             </li>
             <li>
              Less than 0  Returns an array except for the last
              <em>
               -limit
              </em>
              elements()
             </li>
             <li>
              0  Returns an array with one element
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

         10. chr()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           chr()
          </code>
          function returns a character when you pass it an ASCII value.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns a string consisting of the single ASCII character

          ascii
         </strong>
         .

          </strong>

        <h2>
         11. trim()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           trim()
          </code>
          function cleans a string of all whitespace or other specified characters.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         with every whitespace character in
         <strong>
          charlist
         </strong>
         stripped from the beginning and end of the string. You can specify a range of characters to strip using
         <code>
          ..
         </code>
         within the string. For example,
         <code>
          a..z
         </code>
         would strip each lowercase alphabetical character. If
         <strong>
          charlist
         </strong>
         is not supplied, n, r, t, x0B, , and spaces are stripped.
        </p>
        <h3>
         trim function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           trim
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, charlist
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to check
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             charlist
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies which characters to remove from the string. If left out, all of the following characters are removed:
            <ul>
             <li>
                NULL
             </li>
             <li>
              t  tab
             </li>
             <li>
              n  new line
             </li>
             <li>
              x0B  vertical tab
             </li>
             <li>
              r  carriage return
             </li>
             <li>
                 ordinary white space
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>

         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">

$text = ('asdf This is a

 at the start and end,

 asdf');

        <h2>
         12. str_repeat()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           str_repeat()
          </code>
          function repeats a string a specified number of times..
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns a string consisting of
         <strong>
          repeat
         </strong>
         copies of
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         appended to each other. If
         <strong>
          repeat
         </strong>
         is not greater than 0, an empty string is returned.
        </p>
        <h3>
         str_repeat function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           substr
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, repeat
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to repeat
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             repeat
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the number of times the string will be repeated. Must be greater or equal to 0
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>

        <h2>
         13. strtoupper()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strtoupper()
          </code>
          function returns a string with all of its characters converted to uppercase.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         If you know where the information that you want lies in a larger string, you can extract it out with the
         <code>
          strtoupper()
         </code>
         function.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strtoupper function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strtoupper
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to be converted to uppercase.
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         14. str_pad()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           str_pad()
          </code>
          function pads a string to a new length.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Pads
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         using
         <strong>
          pad_string
         </strong>
         until it is at least
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         characters and returns the resulting string. By specifying
         <strong>
          pad_type
         </strong>
         , you can control where the padding occurs..
        </p>
        <h3>
         str_pad function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           str_pad
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, length, pad_string, pad_type
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to pad
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             length
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the new string length. If this value is less than the original length of the string, nothing will be done
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             pad_string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies the string to use for padding. Default is whitespace
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             pad_type
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies what side to pad the string.
            <p>
             Possible values:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              STR_PAD_BOTH  Pad to both sides of the string. If not an even number, the right side gets the extra padding
             </li>
             <li>
              STR_PAD_LEFT  Pad to the left side of the string
             </li>
             <li>
              STR_PAD_RIGHT  Pad to the right side of the string. This is default
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">

               <span class="crayon-ta">

               </span>

        <h2>
         15. ord()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           ord()
          </code>
          function returns the ASCII value of the first character of a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns the ASCII value of the first character in string.
        </p>
        <h3>
         ord function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           ord
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. The string to get an ASCII value from
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d3fa8546701880" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
           &lt;?php
$one = ord('The best way to get an iPhone is to visit your friendly Apple Store');

        <h2>
         16. strtok()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strtok()
          </code>
          function splits a string into smaller strings called tokens.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Breaks string into tokens separated by any of the characters in
         <strong>
          split
         </strong>
         and returns the next
         <br/>
         token found. The first time you call
         <code>
          strtok()
         </code>
         on a string, use the first function prototype; afterward, use the second, providing only the tokens. The function contains an internal pointer for each string it is called with.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strtok function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strtok
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, split
          </em>
          ) and
          <strong>
           strtok
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           split
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to split
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             split
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies one or more split characters
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
           &lt;?php
$string = "Please make sure to follow the instructions (or you'll be put to sleep).";
$token = strtok($string, " ");

while ($token !== false)
{
    echo "$token&lt;br&gt;";
    $token = strtok(" ");
}
?&gt;

        <h2>
         17. strtr()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strtr()
          </code>
          function translates certain characters in a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         When given three arguments, returns a string created by translating in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         every occurrence of a character in
         <strong>
          from
         </strong>
         to the character in
         <strong>
          to
         </strong>
         with the same position. When given two arguments, returns a string created by translating occurrences of the keys in
         <strong>
          array
         </strong>
         in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         with the corresponding values in
         <strong>
          array
         </strong>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         strtr function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strtr
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, from, to
          </em>
          ) and
          <strong>
           strtr
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, array
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to translate
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             from
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Required (unless array is used). Specifies what characters to change
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             to
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Required (unless array is used). Specifies what characters to change into
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             array
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Required (unless to and from is used). An array containing what to change from as key, and what to change to as value
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>

         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">

        <h2>
         18. rtrim()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           rtrim()
          </code>
          function removes whitespace or other predefined characters from the right side of a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         with all characters in
         <strong>
          charlist
         </strong>
         stripped from the end. If
         <strong>
          charlist
         </strong>
         is not specified, the characters stripped are n, r, t, v, , and spaces..
        </p>
        <h3>
         rtrim function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           rtrim
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, charlist
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to check
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             charlist
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies which characters to remove from the string. If left out, all of the following characters are removed:
            <ul>
             <li>
                NULL
             </li>
             <li>
              t  tab
             </li>
             <li>
              n  new line
             </li>
             <li>
              x0B  vertical tab
             </li>
             <li>
              r  carriage return
             </li>
             <li>
                 ordinary white space
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

        <h2>
         19. md5()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           md5()
          </code>
          function calculates the MD5 hash of a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Calculates the MD5 encryption hash of
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         and returns it. If the
         <strong>
          raw
         </strong>
         option is
         <code>
          true
         </code>
         then the MD5 hash returned is in raw binary format (length of 16), binary defaults to
         <code>
          false
         </code>
         , thus making MD5 return a full 32-character hex string.
        </p>
        <h3>
         md5 function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           md5
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, raw
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. The string to be calculated
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             raw
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies hex or binary output format:
            <ul>
             <li>
              TRUE  Raw 16 character binary format
             </li>
             <li>
              FALSE  Default. 32 character hex number
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

        <h2>
         20. strrpos()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strrpos()
          </code>
          function finds the position of the last occurrence of a string inside   another string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns the position of the last occurrence of
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         in string, or false if
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         is not found.
         <br/>
         If specified and positive, the search begins
         <strong>
          start
         </strong>
         characters from the start of string. If specified and negative, the search begins
         <strong>
          start
         </strong>
         characters from the end of string.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strrpos function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strrpos
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, find, start
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             find
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to find
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             start
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies where to begin the search
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

        <h2>
         21. join()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           join()
          </code>
          function returns a string from the elements of an array.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         The
         <code>
          join()
         </code>
         function is simply an alias for
         <code>
          implode()
         </code>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         join function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           join
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           separator, array
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             separator
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies what to put between the array elements.  Default is  (an empty string)
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             array
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. The array to join to a string
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>

        <div class="alert alert-success">
         <strong>
          This @@ does @@ the same @@ thing as implode()
         </strong>
        </div>
        <hr/>
        <h2>
         22. bin2hex()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           bin2hex()
          </code>
          function returns a part of a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Converts
         <code>
          string
         </code>
         to a hexadecimal (base-16) value. Up to a 32-bit number, or 2,147,483,647 decimal, can be converted.
        </p>
        <h3>
         bin2hex function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           bin2hex
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to be converted to hex
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

        <h2>
         23. ltrim()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           ltrim()
          </code>
          function removes whitespace or other predefined characters from the left side of a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         with all characters in
         <strong>
          charlist
         </strong>
         stripped from the beginning. If
         <strong>
          charlist
         </strong>
         is not specified, the characters stripped are n, r, t, v, , and spaces..
        </p>
        <h3>
         ltrim function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           ltrim
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, charlist
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to check
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             charlist
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies which characters to remove from the string. If left out, all of the following characters are removed:
            <ul>
             <li>
                NULL
             </li>
             <li>
              t  tab
             </li>
             <li>
              n  new line
             </li>
             <li>
              x0B  vertical tab
             </li>
             <li>
              r  carriage return
             </li>
             <li>
                 ordinary white space
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d3fd4820603272" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         24. substr_replace()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           substr_replace()
          </code>
          function replaces a part of a string with another string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Replaces a substring in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         with
         <strong>
          replacement
         </strong>
         . The substring replaced is selected using the same rules as those of
         <code>
          substr()
         </code>
         . If string is an array, replacements take place on each string within the array. In this case, replacement, start, and length can either be scalar values, which are used for all strings in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         , or arrays of values to be used for each corresponding value in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         substr_replace function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           substr_replace
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, replacement, start, length
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to check
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             replacement
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to insert
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             start
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies where to start replacing in the string
            <ul>
             <li>
              A positive number  Start replacing at the specified position in the string
             </li>
             <li>
              Negative number  Start replacing at the specified position from the end of the string
             </li>
             <li>
              0  Start replacing at the first character in the string
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             length
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies how many characters should be replaced. Default is the same length as the string.
            <ul>
             <li>
              A positive number  The length of string to be replaced
             </li>
             <li>
              A negative number  How many characters should be left at end of string after replacing
             </li>
             <li>
              0  Insert instead of replace
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d3fdb869308529" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
           &lt;?php
$greet = "Goooooood Morning Vietnam!";
$nyc = substr_replace($greet, "New York!", 18, 7);

echo $nyc.'&lt;br&gt;';

$boston = substr_replace($nyc, "Boston", 18, 8);

echo $boston;
?&gt;
          </textarea>
         </div>

        <h2>
         25. str_split()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           str_split()
          </code>
          function splits a string into an array.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Splits
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         into an array of characters, each containing
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         characters; if
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         is not specified, it defaults to 1.
        </p>
        <h3>
         str_split function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           str_split
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, start, length
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning

        <h2>
         26. sha1()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           sha1()
          </code>
          function returns a part of a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Calculates the sha1 encryption hash of
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         and returns it. If
         <strong>
          raw
         </strong>
         is set and is true, the
         <br/>
         raw binary is returned instead of a hex string.
        </p>
        <h3>
         sha1 function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           sha1
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, raw
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. The string to be calculated
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             raw
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specify hex or binary output format:
            <ul>
             <li>
              TRUE  Raw 20 character binary format
             </li>
             <li>
              FALSE  Default. 40 character hex number
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>

        </p>

        <h2>
         27. ucfirst()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           ucfirst()
          </code>
          function returns a part of a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         with the first character, if alphabetic, converted to uppercase. The table used for converting characters is locale-specific.
        </p>
        <h3>
         ucfirst function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           ucfirst
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to apply an uppercase first letter to.
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         28. chunk_split()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           chunk_split()
          </code>
          function splits a string into a series of smaller parts.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         If you know where the information that you want lies in a larger string, you can extract it out with the
         <code>
          chunk_split()
         </code>
         function.
        </p>
        <h3>
         chunk_split function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           chunk_split
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, length, end
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to split
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             length
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A number that defines the length of the chunks. Default is 76
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             end
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A string that defines what to place at the end of each chunk. Default is rn
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d3ff1286697959" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
           &lt;?php
$sentence = "Eat the Leafy Greens for good health.";

$chunked = chunk_split($sentence, 3, ':-)'); 

echo $chunked;
?&gt;
          </textarea>

        <h2>
         29. ucwords()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           ucwords()
          </code>
          function converts the first character of each word in a string to uppercase.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         If youd like to turn the first character of every word into uppercase, this function will do that for you.
        </p>
        <h3>
         ucwords function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           ucwords
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>

           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to convert to uppercase for the first character of each word.
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         30. htmlspecialchars()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           htmlspecialchars()
          </code>
          function converts some predefined characters to HTML entities.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         When you need to convert actual HTML into the entities that make up that HTML, this function can do that for you.
        </p>
        <h3>
         htmlspecialchars function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           htmlspecialchars
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, flags, character-set, double_encode
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to convert
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             flags
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies how to handle quotes, invalid encoding and the used document type.
            <p>
             The available quote styles are:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              ENT_COMPAT  Default. Encodes only double quotes
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_QUOTES  Encodes double and single quotes
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_NOQUOTES  Does not encode any quotes
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             Invalid encoding:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              ENT_IGNORE  Ignores invalid encoding instead of having the function return an empty string. Should be avoided, as it may have security implications.
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_SUBSTITUTE  Replaces invalid encoding for a specified character set with a Unicode Replacement Character U+FFFD (UTF-8) or &amp;#FFFD; instead of returning an empty string.
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_DISALLOWED  R
              <span lang="no-bok">
               eplaces code points that are invalid in the specified doctype with a Unicode Replacement Character U+FFFD (UTF-8) or &amp;#FFFD;
              </span>
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             Additional flags for specifying the used doctype:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              ENT_HTML401  Default. Handle code as HTML 4.01
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_HTML5  Handle code as HTML 5
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_XML1  Handle code as XML 1
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_XHTML  Handle code as XHTML
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             character-set
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A string that specifies which character-set to use.
            <p>
             Allowed values are:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              UTF-8  Default. ASCII compatible multi-byte 8-bit Unicode
             </li>
             <li>
              ISO-8859-1  Western European
             </li>
             <li>
              ISO-8859-15  Western European (adds the Euro sign + French and Finnish letters missing in ISO-8859-1)
             </li>
             <li>
              cp866  DOS-specific Cyrillic charset
             </li>
             <li>
              cp1251  Windows-specific Cyrillic charset
             </li>
             <li>
              cp1252  Windows specific charset for Western European
             </li>
             <li>
              KOI8-R  Russian
             </li>
             <li>
              BIG5  Traditional Chinese, mainly used in Taiwan
             </li>
             <li>
              GB2312  Simplified Chinese, national standard character set
             </li>
             <li>
              BIG5-HKSCS  Big5 with Hong Kong extensions
             </li>
             <li>
              Shift_JIS  Japanese
             </li>
             <li>
              EUC-JP  Japanese
             </li>
             <li>
              MacRoman  Character-set that was used by Mac OS
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note:
             </strong>
             Unrecognized character-sets will be ignored and replaced by ISO-8859-1 in versions prior to PHP 5.4. As of PHP 5.4, it will be ignored an replaced by UTF-8.
            </p>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             double_encode
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A boolean value that specifies whether to encode existing html entities or not.
            <ul>
             <li>
              TRUE  Default. Will convert everything
             </li>
             <li>
              FALSE  Will not encode existing html entities
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

        <h2>
         31. stripos()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           stripos()
          </code>
          function finds the position of the first occurrence of a string inside another string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns the position of the first occurrence of
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         in string using case-insensitive comparison. If specified, the function begins its search at position
         <strong>
          start
         </strong>
         . Returns false if
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         is not found.
        </p>
        <h3>
         stripos function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           stripos
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, find, start
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             find
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to find
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             start
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies where to begin the search
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>

         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
