        <h2>
         32. substr_count()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           substr_count()
          </code>
          function counts the number of times a substring occurs in a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns the number of times
         <strong>
          substring
         </strong>
         appears in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         . If
         <strong>
          start
         </strong>
         is provided, the search begins at that character offset for at most
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         characters, or until the end of the string if
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         is not provided.
        </p>
        <h3>
         substr_count function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           substr_count
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, substring, start, length
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to check
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             substring
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search for
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             start
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies where in string to start searching
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             length
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies the length of the search
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

        <h2>
         33. number_format()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           number_format()
          </code>
          function formats a number with grouped thousands.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Creates a string representation of
         <strong>
          number
         </strong>
         . If
         <strong>
          decimals
         </strong>
         is given, the number is rounded to that many decimal places; the default is no decimal places, creating an integer. If
         <strong>
          decimalpoint
         </strong>
         and
         <strong>
          separator
         </strong>
         are provided, they are used as the decimal-place character and thousands separator, respectively.
        </p>
        <h3>
         number_format function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           number_format
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           number, decimals, decimalpoint, separator
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             number
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. The number to be formatted. If no other parameters are set, the number will be formatted without decimals and with comma (,) as the thousands separator.
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             decimals
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies how many decimals. If this parameter is set, the number will be formatted with a dot (.) as decimal point
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             decimalpoint
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies what string to use for decimal point
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             separator
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies what string to use for thousands separator. Only the first character of separator is used. For example, xxx will give the same output as x
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note:
             </strong>
             If this parameter is given, all other parameters are required as well
            </p>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

        <h2>
         34. stripcslashes()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           stripcslashes()
          </code>
          function removes backslashes added by the addcslashes() function.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         When you need to clean up data retrieved from a database or from an HTML form, this function works great.
        </p>
        <h3>
         stripcslashes function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           stripcslashes
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to clean.
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">

          Friend what you have is one dirty string
         </strong>

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         35. strstr()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strstr()
          </code>
          function searches for the first occurrence of a string inside another string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns the portion of
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         from the first occurrence of
         <strong>
          search
         </strong>
         until the end of
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         , or from the first occurrence of
         <strong>
          search
         </strong>
         until the beginning of
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         if
         <strong>
          before_search
         </strong>
         is specified
         <br/>
         and true. If
         <strong>
          search
         </strong>
         is not found, the function returns false. If
         <strong>
          search
         </strong>
         contains more than one character, only the first is used.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strstr function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strstr
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, search, before_search
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             search
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search for. If this parameter is a number, it will search for the character matching the ASCII value of the number
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             before_search
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A boolean value whose default is false. If set to true, it returns the part of the string before the first occurrence of the
            <em>
             search
            </em>
            parameter.
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>

        </p>

        <h2>
         36. wordwrap()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           wordwrap()
          </code>
          function wraps a string into new lines when it reaches a specific   length.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Inserts
         <b>
          break
         </b>
         into
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         every
         <b>
          width
         </b>
         characters and at the end of the string and returns the resulting string. While inserting breaks, the function attempts to not break in the middle of a word. If not specified,
         <b>
          break
         </b>
         defaults to n and size defaults to 75. If
         <strong>
          cut
         </strong>
         is given and is true, the string is always wrapped to the given
         <b>
          width
         </b>
        </p>
        <h3>
         wordwrap function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           wordwrap
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, width, break, cut
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to break up into lines
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             width
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies the maximum line width. Default is 75
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             break
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies the characters to use as break. Default is n
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             cut
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies whether words longer than the specified width should be wrapped:
            <ul>
             <li>
              FALSE  Default. No-wrap
             </li>
             <li>
              TRUE  Wrap
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d4021631608726" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
           &lt;?php
$str = "Sometimes you will have a string that is quite long and in cases like that you can use the wordwrap function to make it easier to work with.";

          </textarea>

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         37. addcslashes()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           addcslashes()
          </code>
          function returns a string with backslashes in front of the specified characters.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns escaped instances of
         <strong>
          characters
         </strong>
         in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         by adding a backslash before them. You
         <br/>
         can specify ranges of characters by separating them with two periods; for example, to escape characters between a and q, use "a..q". Multiple characters and ranges can be specified in
         <strong>
          characters
         </strong>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         addcslashes function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           addcslashes
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, characters
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to be escaped
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             characters
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the characters or range of characters to be escaped
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>

          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">

$str = "Hi Traveler, thanks for stopping by!";

        <h2>
         38. parse_str()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           parse_str()
          </code>
          function parses a query string into variables.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Parses
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         as if coming from an HTTP POST request, setting variables in the local scope
         <br/>
         to the values found in the string. If
         <strong>
          array
         </strong>
         is given, the array is set with keys and values from the string.
        </p>
        <h3>
         parse_str function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           parse_str
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, array
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to parse
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             array
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies the name of an array to store the variables. This parameter indicates that the variables will be stored in an array.
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

        <h2>
         39. strcmp()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strcmp()
          </code>
          function compares two strings.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Compares two strings; returns a number less than 0 if stringone is less than stringtwo, 0 if the two strings are equal, and a number greater than 0 if stringone is greater than stringtwo. The comparison is case sensitive meaning, Alphabet and alphabet are not considered equal.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strcmp function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strcmp
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           stringone, stringtwo
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             stringone
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the first string to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             stringtwo
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the second string to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

        <h2>
         40. strip_tags()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strip_tags()
          </code>
          function strips a string from HTML, XML, and PHP tags.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Removes PHP and HTML tags from
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         and returns the result. The
         <strong>
          allow
         </strong>
         parameter can
         <br/>
         be specified to not remove certain tags. The string should be a comma-separated list of the tags to ignore; for example, "&lt;b&gt;,&lt;i&gt;" will leave bold and italic tags.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strip_tags function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strip_tags
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, allow
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to check
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             allow
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies allowable tags. These tags will not be removed
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">

         <strong>
          41. substr_compare() definition: The substr() function returns a part of a string.

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         41. substr_compare()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           substr_compare()
          </code>
          function compares two strings from a specified start position.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Compares
         <strong>
          stringone
         </strong>
         , starting at the position
         <strong>
          startpos
         </strong>
         , to
         <strong>
          stringtwo
         </strong>
         . If
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         is specified, a maximum of that many characters are compared. Finally, if
         <strong>
          case
         </strong>
         is specified and true, the comparison is case-insensitive. Returns a number less than 0 if the substring of
         <strong>
          stringone
         </strong>
         is less than
         <strong>
          stringtwo
         </strong>
         , 0 if they are equal, and a number greater than 0 if the substring of
         <strong>
          stringone
         </strong>
         is greater than
         <strong>
          stringtwo
         </strong>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         substr_compare function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           substr_compare
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           stringone, starttwo, startpos, length, case
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             stringone
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the first string to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             stringtwo
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the second string to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             startpos
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies where to start comparing in string1. If negative, it starts counting from the end of the string
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             length
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies how much of string1 to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             case
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A boolean value that specifies whether or not to perform a case-sensitive compare:
            <ul>
             <li>
              FALSE  Default. Case-sensitive
             </li>
             <li>
              TRUE  Case-insensitive
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d403e055319830" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">

        <h2>
         42. setlocale()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           setlocale()
          </code>
          function sets locale information which refers to language, monetary, time and other information specific for a geographical area.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Sets the locale for
         <strong>
          constant
         </strong>
         functions to
         <strong>
          location
         </strong>
         . Returns the current
         <strong>
          location
         </strong>
         after being set, or false if the
         <strong>
          location
         </strong>
         cannot be set. Any number of options for
         <strong>
          constant
         </strong>
         can be added (or ORed) together.
        </p>
        <h3>
         setlocale function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           setlocale
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           constant, location
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             constant
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies what locale information should be set.
            <p>
             Available constants:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              LC_ALL  All of the below
             </li>
             <li>
              LC_COLLATE  Sort order
             </li>
             <li>
              LC_CTYPE  Character classification and conversion (e.g. all characters should be lower or upper-case)
             </li>
             <li>
              LC_MESSAGES  System message formatting
             </li>
             <li>
              LC_MONETARY  Monetary/currency formatting
             </li>
             <li>
              LC_NUMERIC  Numeric formatting
             </li>
             <li>
              LC_TIME  Date and time formatting
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             location
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies what country/region to set the locale information to. Can be a string or an array. It is possible to pass multiple locations.
            <p>
             If the location is NULL or the empty string , the location names will be set from the values of environment variables with the same names as the constants above, or from LANG.
            </p>
            <p>
             If the location is 0, the location setting is not affected, only the current setting is returned.
            </p>
            <p>
             If the location is an array, setlocale() will try each array element until it finds a valid language or region code. This is very useful if a region is known under different names   	on different systems.
            </p>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d4044564996580" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">

        <h2>
         43. str_ireplace()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           str_ireplace()
          </code>
          function replaces some characters with some other   characters in a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Performs a case-insensitive search for all occurrences of
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         and replaces them
         <br/>
         with
         <strong>
          replace
         </strong>
         . If all three parameters are strings, a string is returned. If
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         is an array, the
         <br/>
         replacement is performed for every element in the array and an array of results is returned. If
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         and
         <strong>
          replace
         </strong>
         are both arrays, elements in
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         are replaced with the elements in
         <strong>
          replace
         </strong>
         with the same numeric indices. Finally, if
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         is an array and
         <strong>
          replace
         </strong>
         is a string, any occurrence of any element in
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         is changed to
         <strong>
          replace
         </strong>
         . If supplied,
         <strong>
          count
         </strong>
         is filled with the number of instances replaced.
        </p>
        <h3>
         str_ireplace function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           str_ireplace
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           find, replace, string, count
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             find
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the value to find
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             replace
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the value to replace the value in
            <em>
             find
            </em>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to be searched
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             count
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A variable that counts the number of replacements
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d404a586657899" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">

        <h2>
         44. strncasecmp()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strncasecmp()
          </code>
          function compares two strings.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Compares two strings; returns a number less than 0 if
         <strong>
          stringone
         </strong>
         is less than
         <strong>
          stringtwo
         </strong>
         , 0 if the two strings are equal, and a number greater than 0 if
         <strong>
          stringone
         </strong>
         is greater than
         <strong>
          stringtwo
         </strong>
         . The comparison is case insensitive meaning, Alphabet and alphabet are considered equal. This function is a case insensitive version of
         <code>
          strcmp()
         </code>
         . If either string is shorter than
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         characters, the length of that string determines how many characters are compared.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strncasecmp function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strncasecmp
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           stringone, stringtwo, length
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             stringone
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the first string to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             stringtwo
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the second string to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             length
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specify the number of characters from each string to be used in the comparison
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

        <h2>
         45. crypt()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           crypt()
          </code>
          function returns a string encrypted using DES, Blowfish, or MD5 algorithms.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Encrypts
         <strong>
          str
         </strong>
         using the DES encryption algorithm seeded with the two-character salt value
         <strong>
          salt
         </strong>
         . If
         <strong>
          salt
         </strong>
         is not supplied, a random salt value is generated the first time
         <code>
          crypt()
         </code>
         is called
         <br/>
         in a script; this value is used on subsequent calls to
         <code>
          crypt()
         </code>
         . Returns the encrypted string.
        </p>
        <h3>
         crypt function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           crypt
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           str, salt
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             str
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to be encoded
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             salt
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A string used to increase the number of characters encoded, to make the encoding more secure. If the salt argument is not provided, one will be randomly generated by PHP each time you call this function.
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

        <h2>
         46. printf()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           printf()
          </code>
          function outputs a formatted string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Outputs a string created by using
         <strong>
          format
         </strong>
         and the given arguments. The arguments are placed into the string in various places denoted by special markers in the format string. Each marker starts with a percent sign (%) and consists of the following elements, in order. Except for the type specifier, the specifiers are all optional. To include a percent sign in the string, use %%.
        </p>
        <h3>
         printf function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           printf
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           format, arg1, arg2, arg++
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             format
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string and how to format the variables in it.
            <p>
             Possible format values:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              %%  Returns a percent sign
             </li>
             <li>
              %b  Binary number
             </li>
             <li>
              %c  The character according to the ASCII value
             </li>
             <li>
              %d  Signed decimal number (negative, zero or positive)
             </li>
             <li>
              %e  Scientific notation using a lowercase (e.g. 1.2e+2)
             </li>
             <li>
              %E  Scientific notation using a uppercase (e.g. 1.2E+2)
             </li>
             <li>
              %u  Unsigned decimal number (equal to or greather than zero)
             </li>
             <li>
              %f  Floating-point number (local settings aware)
             </li>
             <li>
              %F  Floating-point number (not local settings aware)
             </li>
             <li>
              %g  shorter of %e and %f
             </li>
             <li>
              %G  shorter of %E and %f
             </li>
             <li>
              %o  Octal number
             </li>
             <li>
              %s  String
             </li>
             <li>
              %x  Hexadecimal number (lowercase letters)
             </li>
             <li>
              %X  Hexadecimal number (uppercase letters)
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             Additional format values. These are placed between the % and the letter (example %.2f):
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              + (Forces both + and  in front of numbers. By default, only negative numbers are marked)
             </li>
             <li>
               (Specifies what to use as padding. Default is space. Must be used together with the width specifier. Example: %x20s (this uses x as padding)
             </li>
             <li>
               (Left-justifies the variable value)
             </li>
             <li>
              [0-9] (Specifies the minimum width held of to the variable value)
             </li>
             <li>
              .[0-9] (Specifies the number of decimal digits or maximum    		string length)
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note:
             </strong>
             If multiple additional format values are used, they must be in the same order as above.
            </p>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             arg1
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. The argument to be inserted at the first %-sign in the format string
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             arg2
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. The argument to be inserted at the second %-sign in the format string
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             arg++
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. The argument to be inserted at the third, fourth, etc. %-sign in the format string
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d405e491529911" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
           &lt;?php

$fahrenheit = 68;

$celsius = ($fahrenheit - 32) * 5 / 9;
printf("%.2fF is %.2fC", $fahrenheit, $celsius);

              <div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-558b4d16d405e491529911-1">
               <span class="crayon-ta">
                &lt;?php
               </span>
              </div>
              <div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-558b4d16d405e491529911-2">
              </div>
              <div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-558b4d16d405e491529911-3">

        <h2>
         47. quoted_printable_decode()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           quoted_printable_decode()
          </code>
          function decodes a quoted-printable string to   an 8-bit ASCII string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Decodes
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         , which is data encoded using the quoted printable encoding, and returns the resulting string.
        </p>
        <h3>
         quoted_printable_decode function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           quoted_printable_decode
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>

             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>

        <h2>
         48. sscanf()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           sscanf()
          </code>
          function parses input from a string according to a specified format.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         The
         <code>
          sscanf()
         </code>
         function decomposes a string according to a
         <code>
          printf()
         </code>
          like template
        </p>
        <h3>
         sscanf function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           sscanf
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, format, arg1, arg2, arg++
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to read
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             format
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the format to use.
            <p>
             Possible format values:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              %%  Returns a percent sign
             </li>
             <li>
              %c  The character according to the ASCII value
             </li>
             <li>
              %d  Signed decimal number (negative, zero or positive)
             </li>
             <li>
              %e  Scientific notation using a lowercase (e.g. 1.2e+2)
             </li>
             <li>
              %u  Unsigned decimal number (equal to or greather than zero)
             </li>
             <li>
              %f  Floating-point number
             </li>
             <li>
              %o  Octal number
             </li>
             <li>
              %s  String
             </li>
             <li>
              %x  Hexadecimal number (lowercase letters)
             </li>
             <li>
              %X  Hexadecimal number (uppercase letters)
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             Additional format values. These are placed between the % and the letter (example %.2f):
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              + (Forces both + and  in front of numbers. By   	default, only negative numbers are marked)
             </li>
             <li>
               (Specifies what to use as padding. Default is space. Must be used together with the width specifier. Example: %x20s (this uses x as padding)
             </li>
             <li>
               (Left-justifies the variable value)
             </li>
             <li>
              [0-9] (Specifies the minimum width held of to the variable value)
             </li>
             <li>
              .[0-9] (Specifies the number of decimal digits or maximum    		string length)
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note:
             </strong>
             If multiple additional format values are used, they must be in the same order as above.
            </p>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             arg1
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. The first variable to store data in
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             arg2
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. The second variable to store data in
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             arg++
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. The third, fourth, and so on, to store data in
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

        <h2>
         49. crc32()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           crc32()
          </code>
          function calculates a 32-bit CRC (cyclic redundancy checksum) for   a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Calculates and returns the cyclic redundancy checksum (CRC) for
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         crc32 function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           crc32
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. The string to be calculated
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

         Code Example

        <hr/>
        <h2>
         50. htmlentities()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           htmlentities()
          </code>
          function converts characters to HTML entities.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Converts all characters in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         that have special meaning in HTML and returns the resulting string. All entities defined in the HTML standard are converted. If supplied, flags determines the manner in which quotes are translated.
        </p>
        <h3>
         htmlentities function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           htmlentities
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, flags, character-set, double_encode
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to convert
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             flags
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies how to handle quotes, invalid encoding and the used document type.
            <p>
             The available quote styles   	are:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              ENT_COMPAT  Default. Encodes only double quotes
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_QUOTES  Encodes double and single quotes
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_NOQUOTES  Does not encode any quotes
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             Invalid encoding:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              ENT_IGNORE  Ignores invalid encoding instead of having the function return an empty string. Should be avoided, as it may have security   		implications.
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_SUBSTITUTE  Replaces invalid encoding for a specified character set with a Unicode Replacement Character U+FFFD (UTF-8) or &amp;#FFFD;   		instead of returning an empty string.
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_DISALLOWED  R
              <span lang="no-bok">
               eplaces code points that are invalid in the specified doctype with a Unicode Replacement Character   		U+FFFD (UTF-8) or &amp;#FFFD;
              </span>
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             Additional flags for specifying the used doctype:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              ENT_HTML401  Default. Handle code as HTML 4.01
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_HTML5  Handle code as HTML 5
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_XML1  Handle code as XML 1
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_XHTML  Handle code as XHTML
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             character-set
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A string that specifies which character-set to use.
            <p>
             Allowed values are:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              UTF-8  Default. ASCII compatible multi-byte 8-bit Unicode
             </li>
             <li>
              ISO-8859-1  Western European
             </li>
             <li>
              ISO-8859-15  Western European (adds the Euro sign + French and Finnish letters missing in ISO-8859-1)
             </li>
             <li>
              cp866  DOS-specific Cyrillic charset
             </li>
             <li>
              cp1251  Windows-specific Cyrillic charset
             </li>
             <li>
              cp1252  Windows specific charset for Western European
             </li>
             <li>
              KOI8-R  Russian
             </li>
             <li>
              BIG5  Traditional Chinese, mainly used in Taiwan
             </li>
             <li>
              GB2312  Simplified Chinese, national standard character set
             </li>
             <li>
              BIG5-HKSCS  Big5 with Hong Kong extensions
             </li>
             <li>
              Shift_JIS  Japanese
             </li>
             <li>
              EUC-JP  Japanese
             </li>
             <li>
              MacRoman  Character-set that was used by Mac OS
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note:
             </strong>
             Unrecognized character-sets will be ignored and replaced by ISO-8859-1 in versions prior to PHP 5.4. As of PHP 5.4, it will be ignored   	an replaced by UTF-8.
            </p>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             double_encode
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A boolean value that specifies whether to encode existing html entities or not.
            <ul>
             <li>
              TRUE  Default. Will convert everything
             </li>
             <li>
              FALSE  Will not encode existing html entities
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

        <h2>
         51. levenshtein()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           levenshtein()
          </code>
          function returns the Levenshtein distance between two   strings.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Calculates the Levenshtein distance between two strings. This is the number of characters you have to replace, insert, or delete to transform
         <strong>
          stringone
         </strong>
         into
         <strong>
          stringtwo
         </strong>
         . By default, replacements, inserts, and deletes have the same cost, but you can specify different costs with
         <strong>
          insert
         </strong>
         ,
         <strong>
          replace
         </strong>
         , and
         <strong>
          delete
         </strong>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         levenshtein function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           levenshtein
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           stringone, stringtwo, insert, replace, delete
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             stringone
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. First string to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             stringtwo
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Second string to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             insert
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. The cost of inserting a character. Default is 1
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             replace
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. The cost of replacing a character. Default is 1
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             delete
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. The cost of deleting a character. Default is 1
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->
        <div class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-github crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-always" id="crayon-558b4d16d407d487662968" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">

           &lt;?php

              <div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-558b4d16d407d487662968-1">
               <span class="crayon-ta">
                &lt;?php
               </span>
              </div>
              <div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-558b4d16d407d487662968-2">

               <span class="crayon-ta">
                ?&gt;
               </span>
              </div>
             </div>
            </td>
           </tr>
          </table>
         </div>
        </div>

         </strong>

        <h2>
         52. strcasecmp()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strcasecmp()
          </code>
          function compares two strings.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Compares two strings; returns a number less than 0 if
         <strong>
          stringone
         </strong>
         is less than
         <strong>
          stringtwo
         </strong>
         , 0 if the two strings are equal, and a number greater than 0 if
         <strong>
          stringone
         </strong>
         is greater than
         <strong>
          stringtwo
         </strong>
         . The comparison is case insensitive meaning, Alphabet and alphabet are considered equal.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strcasecmp function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strcasecmp
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           stringone, stringtwo
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             stringone
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the first string to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             stringtwo
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the second string to compare
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>
        <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

         <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
          <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly="" style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 18px !important;" wrap="soft">
           &lt;?php
echo strcasecmp("Awesome", "Awesome");
echo "&lt;br&gt;";
echo strcasecmp("AwEsOmE", "awesome");
?&gt;
          </textarea>

        <h2>
         53. strcspn()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strcspn()
          </code>
          function returns the number of characters (including   whitespaces) found in a string   before any part of the specified characters are found.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns the length of the subset of
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         starting at
         <strong>
          start
         </strong>
         , examining a maximum of
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         characters, to the first instance of a character from
         <strong>
          char
         </strong>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         strcspn function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strcspn
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, char, start, length
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             char
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the characters to search for
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             start
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies where in string to start
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             length
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies the length of the string (how much of the string to search)
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

         Code Example
        </h4>

        <h2>
         54. strripos()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strripos()
          </code>
          function finds the position of the last occurrence of a string inside   another string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns the position of the last occurrence of
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         in string using a case-insensitive search,
         <br/>
         or false if
         <strong>
          find
         </strong>
         is not found. If specified and positive, the search begins
         <strong>
          start
         </strong>
         characters
         <br/>
         from the start of string. If specified and negative, the search begins
         <strong>
          start
         </strong>
         characters from
         <br/>
         the end of string. This function is a case-insensitive version of
         <code>
          strrpos()
         </code>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         strripos function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strripos
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, find, start
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             find
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to find
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             start
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies where to begin the search
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>

        <h2>
         55. strspn()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strspn()
          </code>
          function returns the number of characters found in the string that contains only characters from the charlist parameter.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns the length of the substring in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         that consists solely of characters in
         <strong>
          charlist
         </strong>
         . If
         <strong>
          start
         </strong>
         is positive, the search starts at that character; if it is negative, the substring starts at the character
         <strong>
          start
         </strong>
         characters from the strings end. If
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         is given and is positive, that many characters from the start of the substring are checked. If
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         is given and is negative, the check ends
         <strong>
          length
         </strong>
         characters from the end of string.
        </p>
        <h3>
         strspn function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strspn
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, charlist, start, length
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             charlist
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the characters to find
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             start
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies where in the string to start
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             length
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Defines the length of the string
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <h4>
         Code Example
        </h4>
        <p>
        </p>

        <h2>
         56. html_entity_decode()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           html_entity_decode()
          </code>
          function converts HTML entities to characters.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Converts all HTML entities in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         to the equivalent character. All entities defined in the HTML standard are converted. If supplied,
         <strong>
          flags
         </strong>
         determines the manner in which quotes are translated. The possible values for
         <strong>
          flags
         </strong>
         are the same as those for htmlentities. If supplied,
         <strong>
          character-set
         </strong>
         determines the final encoding for the characters. The possible values for
         <strong>
          character-set
         </strong>
         are the same as those for htmlentities.
        </p>
        <h3>
         html_entity_decode function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           html_entity_decode
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, flags, character-se
          </em>
          t)
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to decode
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             flags
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. Specifies how to handle quotes and which document type to use.
            <p>
             The available quote styles are:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              ENT_COMPAT  Default. Decodes only double quotes
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_QUOTES  Decodes double and single quotes
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_NOQUOTES  Does not decode any quotes
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             Additional flags for specifying the used doctype:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              ENT_HTML401  Default. Handle code as HTML 4.01
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_HTML5  Handle code as HTML 5
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_XML1  Handle code as XML 1
             </li>
             <li>
              ENT_XHTML  Handle code as XHTML
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             character-set
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A string that specifies which character-set to   	use.
            <p>
             Allowed values are:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              UTF-8  Default. ASCII compatible multi-byte 8-bit Unicode
             </li>
             <li>
              ISO-8859-1  Western European
             </li>
             <li>
              ISO-8859-15  Western European (adds the Euro sign + French and Finnish letters missing in ISO-8859-1)
             </li>
             <li>
              cp866  DOS-specific Cyrillic charset
             </li>
             <li>
              cp1251  Windows-specific Cyrillic charset
             </li>
             <li>
              cp1252  Windows specific charset for Western European
             </li>
             <li>
              KOI8-R  Russian
             </li>
             <li>
              BIG5  Traditional Chinese, mainly used in Taiwan
             </li>
             <li>
              GB2312  Simplified Chinese, national standard character set
             </li>
             <li>
              BIG5-HKSCS  Big5 with Hong Kong extensions
             </li>
             <li>
              Shift_JIS  Japanese
             </li>
             <li>
              EUC-JP  Japanese
             </li>
             <li>
              MacRoman  Character-set that was used by Mac OS
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

        <h2>
         57. str_shuffle()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           str_shuffle()
          </code>
          function randomly shuffles all the characters of a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Rearranges the characters in string into a random order and returns the resulting string.
        </p>

          </strong>
          (

        <h2>
         58. stristr()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           stristr()
          </code>
          searches for the first occurrence of a string inside another string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         This is the case insensitive version of
         <code>
          strstr()
         </code>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         stristr function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           stristr
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, search, before_search
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th>
            Argument
           </th>
           <th>
            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             search
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search for. If this parameter is a number, it will search for the character matching the ASCII value of the number
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             before_search
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Not Mandatory. A boolean value whose default is false. If set to true, it returns the part of the string before the first occurrence of the
            <em>
             search
            </em>
            parameter.
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

        <h2>
         59. strpbrk()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strpbrk()
          </code>
          function searches a string for any of the specified characters.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         Returns a string consisting of the substring of
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         , starting from the position of the first instance of a character from charlist in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         to the end of the string, or false if none of the characters in charlist is found in
         <strong>
          string
         </strong>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         strpbrk function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strpbrk
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string, charlist
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>
        <p>
        </p>
        <table class="table table-striped table-hover">

            Argument Meaning
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             string
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the string to search
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td>
            <em>
             charlist
            </em>
           </td>
           <td>
            Mandatory. Specifies the characters to find
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

        <h2>
         60. strrev()
         <small>
          <strong>
           definition:
          </strong>
          The
          <code>
           strrev()
          </code>
          function reverses a string.
         </small>
        </h2>
        <p>
         <span class="label label-info">
          <strong>
           Usage:
          </strong>
         </span>
         If you need to know how to spell something backwards, this is the function for you..
        </p>
        <h3>
         strrev function signature
         <small>
          <strong>
           strrev
          </strong>
          (
          <em>
           string
          </em>
          )
         </small>
        </h3>

        </p>
